"""Custom top-k kernel for RTX 3090 (SM86).

Returns the k largest values per row of a (batch, n) fp32 tensor, sorted
descending, with their int64 indices -- same contract as the reference, but
implemented from scratch in CUDA (no library selection/sort calls).

Design
------
The deck is bandwidth/launch bound: each row read is tiny (0.5-2 MB), so the
wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel launch/dispatch overhead and cold-DRAM
latency, not the selection compute. Levers:

  1. A custom kernel (block-per-row, templated on K). Each thread streams its
     slice with vectorized float4 loads and keeps a register-resident sorted
     top-K buffer, updated with a *branchless, compile-time-indexed* insertion
     so the buffer never spills to local memory.
       - K<=32: lanes are reduced by a warp-shuffle butterfly using an in-place
         bitonic top-K merge (C[i]=max(A[i],B[K-1-i]) is bitonic; bitonic-sort
         it), so only T/32 partials hit shared memory -> high occupancy.
       - K==64: the warp bitonic merge would need 256 registers and spill to
         (DRAM-backed) local memory, which is ruinous on the cold path, so the
         block reduces all T lists through a shared-memory merge-tree instead.
     For the single very-large row (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot saturate
     DRAM, so the row is split across BPR blocks (each emits a partial top-K)
     and a second tiny kernel merges the partials.

  2. Reusable output buffers (allocated once per Model) plus CUDA-graph
     capture/replay, which collapses per-call launch + Python dispatch overhead
     to a single graph launch. Replay reads live memory at the captured input
     pointer, so it stays correct as the input data changes between calls.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

_CUDA_SRC = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <ATen/cuda/CUDAContext.h>
#include <c10/cuda/CUDAStream.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cfloat>

// Branchless insert of (v, idx) into a descending register-resident top-K
// buffer (drops the current min). All indices are compile-time so tv/ti stay
// in registers.
template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void insert(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int idx) {
    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
    float pv = v;  int pi = idx;
    #pragma unroll
    for (int p = 0; p < K; ++p) {
        bool take = (pv > tv[p]);
        float cur_v = tv[p];  int cur_i = ti[p];
        tv[p] = take ? pv : cur_v;
        ti[p] = take ? pi : cur_i;
        pv = take ? cur_v : pv;
        pi = take ? cur_i : pi;
    }
}

// Merge two descending length-K lists (A,B) -> top-K of union into (ov,oi).
template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void merge2(
    const float* Av, const int* Ai, const float* Bv, const int* Bi,
    float* ov, int* oi) {
    int i = 0, j = 0;
    #pragma unroll
    for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) {
        float a = Av[i], b = Bv[j];
        if (a >= b) { ov[m] = a; oi[m] = Ai[i]; ++i; }
        else        { ov[m] = b; oi[m] = Bi[j]; ++j; }
    }
}

// Warp reduction: 32 lanes each hold a descending top-K in registers; butterfly
// shuffle so lane 0 ends with the warp-wide top-K.  Each step merges two
// descending K-lists in place via the bitonic top-K trick
// (C[i] = max(A[i], B[K-1-i]) is bitonic and holds the top-K; bitonic-sort it),
// which needs only the received list as scratch (4K regs, no 6K two-pointer).
template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void warp_merge(float* tv, int* ti) {
    #pragma unroll
    for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
        float rv[K]; int ri[K];
        #pragma unroll
        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) {
            rv[m] = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, tv[m], off);
            ri[m] = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, ti[m], off);
        }
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < K; ++i) {
            int j = K - 1 - i;
            if (rv[j] > tv[i]) { tv[i] = rv[j]; ti[i] = ri[j]; }
        }
        #pragma unroll
        for (int s = K >> 1; s >= 1; s >>= 1) {
            #pragma unroll
            for (int i = 0; i < K; ++i) {
                int p = i ^ s;
                if (p > i && tv[i] < tv[p]) {
                    float fv = tv[i]; tv[i] = tv[p]; tv[p] = fv;
                    int   gi = ti[i]; ti[i] = ti[p]; ti[p] = gi;
                }
            }
        }
    }
}

// In-shared merge-tree: T lists of length K (one per thread) -> list 0 holds
// the block-wide top-K, sorted descending.
template <int K>
__device__ __forceinline__ void block_merge(float* sval, int* sidx, int T, int tid) {
    for (int stride = 1; stride < T; stride <<= 1) {
        __syncthreads();
        if ((tid & ((stride << 1) - 1)) == 0 && (tid + stride) < T) {
            float ov[K]; int oi[K];
            merge2<K>(sval + tid * K, sidx + tid * K,
                      sval + (tid + stride) * K, sidx + (tid + stride) * K, ov, oi);
            #pragma unroll
            for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval[tid * K + m] = ov[m]; sidx[tid * K + m] = oi[m]; }
        }
    }
    __syncthreads();
}

// Block kernel: grid = batch * bpr.  Each block reduces its segment to top-K.
template <int K>
__global__ void topk_block_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ x,
    float* __restrict__ out_val, long long* __restrict__ out_idx,
    float* __restrict__ inter_val, int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
    int n, int bpr) {

    extern __shared__ unsigned char smem[];
    // K<=32 stores one list per warp (T/32 lists); K==64 stores one per thread.
    int nlists = (K <= 32) ? ((blockDim.x >> 5) < 1 ? 1 : (blockDim.x >> 5)) : blockDim.x;
    float* sval = reinterpret_cast<float*>(smem);
    int*   sidx = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sval + nlists * K);

    const int T = blockDim.x, tid = threadIdx.x;
    const int row = blockIdx.x / bpr, seg = blockIdx.x % bpr;
    const int base = n / bpr;
    const int start = seg * base;
    const int end = (seg == bpr - 1) ? n : start + base;
    const float* xr = x + (long long)row * n;

    float tv[K]; int ti[K];
    #pragma unroll
    for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = -FLT_MAX; ti[m] = 0; }

    // Vectorized float4 scan.  Issue 4 independent float4 loads before any
    // insert so the cold-DRAM reads overlap (memory-level parallelism), which
    // is the limiter on these tiny transfers.  Segments start on a 16-byte
    // boundary for the canonical shapes; if not, fall back to scalar.
    bool aligned = ((((uintptr_t)(xr + start)) & 15u) == 0);
    if (aligned) {
        const float4* x4 = reinterpret_cast<const float4*>(xr + start);
        int n4 = (end - start) >> 2;
        int vi = tid;
        for (; vi + 3 * T < n4; vi += 4 * T) {
            float4 f0 = __ldg(x4 + vi);
            float4 f1 = __ldg(x4 + vi + T);
            float4 f2 = __ldg(x4 + vi + 2 * T);
            float4 f3 = __ldg(x4 + vi + 3 * T);
            int b0 = start + (vi << 2), b1 = start + ((vi + T) << 2);
            int b2 = start + ((vi + 2 * T) << 2), b3 = start + ((vi + 3 * T) << 2);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f0.x, b0 + 0); insert<K>(tv, ti, f0.y, b0 + 1);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f0.z, b0 + 2); insert<K>(tv, ti, f0.w, b0 + 3);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f1.x, b1 + 0); insert<K>(tv, ti, f1.y, b1 + 1);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f1.z, b1 + 2); insert<K>(tv, ti, f1.w, b1 + 3);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f2.x, b2 + 0); insert<K>(tv, ti, f2.y, b2 + 1);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f2.z, b2 + 2); insert<K>(tv, ti, f2.w, b2 + 3);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f3.x, b3 + 0); insert<K>(tv, ti, f3.y, b3 + 1);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f3.z, b3 + 2); insert<K>(tv, ti, f3.w, b3 + 3);
        }
        for (; vi < n4; vi += T) {
            float4 f = __ldg(x4 + vi);
            int base = start + (vi << 2);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f.x, base + 0); insert<K>(tv, ti, f.y, base + 1);
            insert<K>(tv, ti, f.z, base + 2); insert<K>(tv, ti, f.w, base + 3);
        }
        for (int i = start + (n4 << 2) + tid; i < end; i += T) insert<K>(tv, ti, __ldg(xr + i), i);
    } else {
        for (int i = start + tid; i < end; i += T) insert<K>(tv, ti, __ldg(xr + i), i);
    }

    // K<=32: reduce 32 lanes per warp with shuffles (no shared), then only the
    // W=T/32 warp leaders hit shared.  K==64 would need 256 regs in the warp
    // bitonic merge and spill to (DRAM-backed) local memory -- ruinous on the
    // cold path -- so route it through the all-lists shared merge-tree instead.
    if constexpr (K <= 32) {
        warp_merge<K>(tv, ti);
        const int lane = tid & 31, warp = tid >> 5, W = T >> 5;
        if (lane == 0) {
            #pragma unroll
            for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval[warp * K + m] = tv[m]; sidx[warp * K + m] = ti[m]; }
        }
        block_merge<K>(sval, sidx, W, tid);
    } else {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval[tid * K + m] = tv[m]; sidx[tid * K + m] = ti[m]; }
        block_merge<K>(sval, sidx, T, tid);
    }

    if (bpr == 1) {
        for (int m = tid; m < K; m += T) {
            out_val[(long long)row * K + m] = sval[m];
            out_idx[(long long)row * K + m] = (long long)sidx[m];
        }
    } else {
        for (int m = tid; m < K; m += T) {
            long long off = ((long long)row * bpr + seg) * K + m;
            inter_val[off] = sval[m];
            inter_idx[off] = sidx[m];
        }
    }
}

// Merge kernel: grid = batch, blockDim = padded multiple of 32 >= bpr.
// Each thread loads one partial top-K list (padding lanes load -inf), then the
// same warp + cross-warp reduction yields the row's final top-K.
template <int K>
__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ inter_val, const int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
    float* __restrict__ out_val, long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int bpr) {

    extern __shared__ unsigned char smem[];
    int nlists = (K <= 32) ? ((blockDim.x >> 5) < 1 ? 1 : (blockDim.x >> 5)) : blockDim.x;
    float* sval = reinterpret_cast<float*>(smem);
    int*   sidx = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sval + nlists * K);

    const int T = blockDim.x, tid = threadIdx.x, row = blockIdx.x;

    float tv[K]; int ti[K];
    if (tid < bpr) {
        long long off = ((long long)row * bpr + tid) * K;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = inter_val[off + m]; ti[m] = inter_idx[off + m]; }
    } else {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = -FLT_MAX; ti[m] = 0; }
    }

    if constexpr (K <= 32) {
        warp_merge<K>(tv, ti);
        const int lane = tid & 31, warp = tid >> 5, W = T >> 5;
        if (lane == 0) {
            #pragma unroll
            for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval[warp * K + m] = tv[m]; sidx[warp * K + m] = ti[m]; }
        }
        block_merge<K>(sval, sidx, W, tid);
    } else {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval[tid * K + m] = tv[m]; sidx[tid * K + m] = ti[m]; }
        block_merge<K>(sval, sidx, T, tid);
    }

    for (int m = tid; m < K; m += T) {
        out_val[(long long)row * K + m] = sval[m];
        out_idx[(long long)row * K + m] = (long long)sidx[m];
    }
}

#define LAUNCH(KK)                                                                 \
    if (smem > 48 * 1024)                                                          \
        cudaFuncSetAttribute((const void*)topk_block_kernel<KK>,                   \
            cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, (int)smem);               \
    topk_block_kernel<KK><<<total, (int)threads, smem, stream>>>(                  \
        x.data_ptr<float>(), out_val.data_ptr<float>(),                           \
        reinterpret_cast<long long*>(out_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>()),                \
        inter_val.data_ptr<float>(), inter_idx.data_ptr<int>(), (int)n, (int)bpr); \
    if (bpr > 1) {                                                                 \
        int mergeT = ((int)bpr + 31) & ~31; if (mergeT < 32) mergeT = 32;          \
        int mlists = (KK <= 32) ? (mergeT >> 5) : mergeT;                          \
        size_t smem2 = (size_t)mlists * KK * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int));        \
        if (smem2 > 48 * 1024)                                                     \
            cudaFuncSetAttribute((const void*)topk_merge_kernel<KK>,               \
                cudaFuncAttributeMaxDynamicSharedMemorySize, (int)smem2);          \
        topk_merge_kernel<KK><<<(int)batch, mergeT, smem2, stream>>>(              \
            inter_val.data_ptr<float>(), inter_idx.data_ptr<int>(),               \
            out_val.data_ptr<float>(),                                            \
            reinterpret_cast<long long*>(out_idx.data_ptr<int64_t>()), (int)bpr); \
    }

void topk_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor out_val, torch::Tensor out_idx,
                  torch::Tensor inter_val, torch::Tensor inter_idx,
                  int64_t batch, int64_t n, int64_t k, int64_t bpr, int64_t threads) {
    cudaStream_t stream = at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream();
    int total = (int)(batch * bpr);
    int warps = (int)threads / 32; if (warps < 1) warps = 1;
    int blists = (k <= 32) ? warps : (int)threads;
    size_t smem = (size_t)blists * k * (sizeof(float) + sizeof(int));
    switch (k) {
        case 1:  { LAUNCH(1);  break; }
        case 8:  { LAUNCH(8);  break; }
        case 16: { LAUNCH(16); break; }
        case 32: { LAUNCH(32); break; }
        case 64: { LAUNCH(64); break; }
        default: TORCH_CHECK(false, "unsupported k=", k);
    }
}
"""

_CPP_DECL = (
    "void topk_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor out_val, torch::Tensor out_idx, "
    "torch::Tensor inter_val, torch::Tensor inter_idx, "
    "int64_t batch, int64_t n, int64_t k, int64_t bpr, int64_t threads);"
)

_mod = load_inline(
    name="topk_sm86_v8",
    cpp_sources=_CPP_DECL,
    cuda_sources=_CUDA_SRC,
    functions=["topk_forward"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "-gencode", "arch=compute_86,code=sm_86"],
    extra_cflags=["-O3"],
    verbose=False,
)


def _next_pow2(v: int) -> int:
    p = 1
    while p < v:
        p <<= 1
    return p


# Tuned (threads, bpr) per exact canonical shape, picked from a graph + L2-flush
# sweep on the RTX 3090. Falls back to a heuristic for any other shape.
_TUNED = {
    (1, 131072, 64): (64, 32),   # k64 uses the shared merge-tree (no warp spill)
    (64, 8192, 8):   (256, 1),
    (32, 16384, 32): (128, 2),
    (16, 12000, 16): (64, 8),
    (128, 4096, 1):  (256, 1),
}


def _threads_for_k(k: int) -> int:
    # k==64 takes the all-lists shared merge path; cap T so T*K*8 <= 32KB.
    return {1: 256, 8: 256, 16: 128, 32: 128, 64: 64}.get(k, 128)


def _config_for(batch: int, n: int, k: int) -> tuple[int, int]:
    if (batch, n, k) in _TUNED:
        return _TUNED[(batch, n, k)]
    threads = _threads_for_k(k)
    target = 192
    bpr = _next_pow2(max(1, target // batch))
    bpr = min(bpr, max(1, n // max(1, threads)))   # keep >= ~1 elem/thread
    bpr = min(bpr, 64)                             # bound merge-kernel work
    return threads, max(1, bpr)


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, batch: int, n: int, k: int):
        super().__init__()
        self.batch, self.n, self.k = batch, n, k
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1))
        self.threads, self.bpr = _config_for(batch, n, k)
        self._ready = False
        self._graph = None
        self._graph_key = None
        self._use_graph = True

    def _alloc(self, device):
        b, k, bpr = self.batch, self.k, self.bpr
        self.out_val = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
        self.out_idx = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
        sz = b * bpr * k if bpr > 1 else 1
        self.inter_val = torch.empty(sz, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
        self.inter_idx = torch.empty(sz, dtype=torch.int32, device=device)
        self._ready = True

    def _run(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        _mod.topk_forward(
            x, self.out_val, self.out_idx, self.inter_val, self.inter_idx,
            self.batch, self.n, self.k, self.bpr, self.threads,
        )

    def _capture(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        # Warm up on a side stream (PyTorch CUDA-graph capture protocol), then
        # record the kernel launches into a graph that reads from x's pointer
        # and writes the reusable output buffers.
        s = torch.cuda.Stream()
        s.wait_stream(torch.cuda.current_stream())
        with torch.cuda.stream(s):
            for _ in range(2):
                self._run(x)
        torch.cuda.current_stream().wait_stream(s)
        self._x_ref = x  # keep the captured input alive
        g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
        with torch.cuda.graph(g):
            self._run(x)
        self._graph = g

    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
        if not self._ready:
            self._alloc(x.device)

        if not (self._use_graph and x.is_cuda):
            self._run(x)
            return self.out_val, self.out_idx

        key = (x.data_ptr(), tuple(x.shape))
        if self._graph_key != key:
            try:
                self._capture(x)
                self._graph_key = key
            except Exception:
                # Capture failed -> fall back to eager launches for good.
                self._use_graph = False
                self._graph = None
                self._run(x)
                return self.out_val, self.out_idx
        self._graph.replay()
        return self.out_val, self.out_idx


def get_inputs():
    x = torch.randn(batch, n, dtype=torch.float32)
    return [x]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [batch, n, k]

2	display_name: "TopK via Bitonic Sort"

6	# Top-k is dominated by the input read (small output, no reduction over k).
7	# Comparator-network FLOPs are not the bottleneck on real hardware, so we
8	# track them but score on bandwidth.
9	flops_formula: "batch * n * 4"            # ~O(n log^2 n) compares total, but the
10	                                          # bitonic network is so cheap relative
11	                                          # to memory that a coarse 4*n estimate
12	                                          # is fine for telemetry only.

18

1	"""SOTA reference for TopK: torch.topk itself.
2	
3	torch.topk dispatches to a CUB-backed kernel that uses radix-select for
4	moderate k and a tuned bitonic sort for small n. It is the bar the agent's
5	hand-rolled bitonic kernel must beat. There is no obvious vendor library that
6	does better on the (batch, n, k) shape mix we evaluate — Faiss BlockSelect is
7	specialized for k>=32 with much larger n, and CUB's DeviceSegmentedRadixSort
8	sorts the full row (overkill for top-k).
9	
10	This file is INTENTIONALLY allowed to call torch.topk because it is the SOTA
11	oracle, not the agent's submission. The agent's solution.py is forbidden from
12	using torch.topk (see problem.yaml.forbidden).
13	"""
14	from __future__ import annotations
15	
16	import torch
17	
18	
19	def sota_forward(x: torch.Tensor, k: int):
20	    """Best-available top-k reference. x: (batch, n) fp32."""
21	    return torch.topk(x, k=k, dim=-1, largest=True, sorted=True)
22	
23	
24	def is_available() -> bool:
25	    return True

stdout (4682 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.
2	
3	All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
4	implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.
5	
6	Methodology:
7	  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
8	    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
9	  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
10	    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
11	    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
12	  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
13	    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
14	  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.
15	
16	Notes / known biases not addressed here:
17	  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
18	    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
19	    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
20	    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
21	    "compiled" baseline policy.
22	  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
23	  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
24	    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
25	    instrumentation if you ever care.
26	"""
27	from __future__ import annotations
28	
29	import os
30	import re

1	"""Roofline math: achieved TFLOPS / GB/s, peak fraction.
2	
3	FLOPS and bytes formulas come from the problem's `problem.yaml`. They are the
4	dense-equivalent algorithmic work; kernels that skip work (sparsity, early
5	exit) are still measured against the dense cost.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	
10	def compute_tflops(flops: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
11	    """flops per invocation and wall time in ms -> TFLOPS."""
12	    if time_ms <= 0:
13	        return 0.0
14	    return flops / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
15	
16	
17	def compute_gbps(bytes_moved: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
18	    """bytes per invocation and wall time in ms -> GB/s."""
19	    if time_ms <= 0:
20	        return 0.0
21	    return bytes_moved / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e9
22	
23	
24	def peak_fraction(
25	    achieved: float,
26	    peak: float,
27	) -> float:
28	    """Return achieved / peak, clamped to [0, infinity)."""
29	    if peak <= 0:
30	        return 0.0
31	    return max(0.0, achieved / peak)

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic/solution.py

+"""Custom top-k kernel for RTX 3090 (SM86).
+
+Returns the k largest values per row of a (batch, n) fp32 tensor, sorted
+descending, with their int64 indices -- same contract as the reference, but
+implemented from scratch in CUDA (no library selection/sort calls).
+
+Design
+------
+The deck is bandwidth/launch bound: each row read is tiny (0.5-2 MB), so the
+wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel-launch + dispatch overhead, not by the
+selection compute. Two levers:
+
+  1. A lean single custom kernel (block-per-row) that reads each element once
+     and keeps a per-thread local top-k, then a shared-memory merge-tree
+     reduces the block to its top-k.  For the single very-large row
+     (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot saturate DRAM, so the row is split
+     across BPR blocks (each emits a partial top-k) and a second tiny kernel
+     merges the BPR partials.
+
+  2. Reusable output buffers (allocated once per Model) plus optional CUDA-graph
+     capture/replay, which collapses per-call launch + Python dispatch overhead
+     to a single graph launch -- the dominant cost on these shapes.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
+
+_CUDA_SRC = r"""
+#include <torch/extension.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+#include <cfloat>
+
+#define MAXK 64
+
+// Merge two descending top-k lists (A,B) -> top-k of the union, into (ov,oi).
+__device__ __forceinline__ void merge2(
+    const float* Av, const int* Ai,
+    const float* Bv, const int* Bi,
+    float* ov, int* oi, int k) {
+    int i = 0, j = 0;
+    #pragma unroll 1
+    for (int m = 0; m < k; ++m) {
+        float a = Av[i], b = Bv[j];
+        if (a >= b) { ov[m] = a; oi[m] = Ai[i]; ++i; }
+        else        { ov[m] = b; oi[m] = Bi[j]; ++j; }
+    }
+}
+
+// In-shared merge-tree: T lists of length k (one per thread) -> list 0 holds
+// the block-wide top-k, sorted descending.
+__device__ __forceinline__ void block_merge(
+    float* sval, int* sidx, int k, int T, int tid) {
+    for (int stride = 1; stride < T; stride <<= 1) {
+        __syncthreads();
+        if ((tid & ((stride << 1) - 1)) == 0 && (tid + stride) < T) {
+            float ov[MAXK]; int oi[MAXK];
+            merge2(sval + tid * k, sidx + tid * k,
+                   sval + (tid + stride) * k, sidx + (tid + stride) * k,
+                   ov, oi, k);
+            #pragma unroll 1
+            for (int m = 0; m < k; ++m) {
+                sval[tid * k + m] = ov[m];
+                sidx[tid * k + m] = oi[m];
+            }
+        }
+    }
+    __syncthreads();
+}
+
+// Per-thread insertion of (v, idx) into a descending local top-k buffer.
+__device__ __forceinline__ void insert(float* tv, int* ti, float& tmin,
+                                        float v, int idx, int k) {
+    if (v <= tmin) return;
+    int p = k - 1;
+    tv[p] = v; ti[p] = idx;
+    while (p > 0 && tv[p] > tv[p - 1]) {
+        float fv = tv[p]; tv[p] = tv[p - 1]; tv[p - 1] = fv;
+        int   ii = ti[p]; ti[p] = ti[p - 1]; ti[p - 1] = ii;
+        --p;
+    }
+    tmin = tv[k - 1];
+}
+
+// Block kernel: grid = batch * bpr.  Each block reduces its segment to top-k.
+// bpr == 1 -> write final (float value, int64 index).
+// bpr  > 1 -> write partial to inter buffers (float value, int32 index).
+__global__ void topk_block_kernel(
+    const float* __restrict__ x,
+    float* __restrict__ out_val,
+    long long* __restrict__ out_idx,
+    float* __restrict__ inter_val,
+    int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
+    int n, int k, int bpr) {
+
+    extern __shared__ unsigned char smem[];
+    float* sval = reinterpret_cast<float*>(smem);
+    int*   sidx = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sval + blockDim.x * k);
+
+    const int T   = blockDim.x;
+    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    const int row = blockIdx.x / bpr;
+    const int seg = blockIdx.x % bpr;
+
+    const int base = n / bpr;
+    const int start = seg * base;
+    const int end   = (seg == bpr - 1) ? n : start + base;
+    const float* xr = x + (long long)row * n;
+
+    float tv[MAXK]; int ti[MAXK];
+    #pragma unroll 1
+    for (int m = 0; m < k; ++m) { tv[m] = -FLT_MAX; ti[m] = 0; }
+    float tmin = -FLT_MAX;
+
+    for (int i = start + tid; i < end; i += T) {
+        insert(tv, ti, tmin, __ldg(xr + i), i, k);
+    }
+
+    // publish this thread's local top-k to shared
+    #pragma unroll 1
+    for (int m = 0; m < k; ++m) { sval[tid * k + m] = tv[m]; sidx[tid * k + m] = ti[m]; }
+
+    block_merge(sval, sidx, k, T, tid);
+
+    if (tid < k) {
+        if (bpr == 1) {
+            out_val[(long long)row * k + tid] = sval[tid];
+            out_idx[(long long)row * k + tid] = (long long)sidx[tid];
+        } else {
+            long long off = ((long long)row * bpr + seg) * k + tid;
+            inter_val[off] = sval[tid];
+            inter_idx[off] = sidx[tid];
+        }
+    }
+}
+
+// Merge kernel: grid = batch, blockDim = bpr.  Combine bpr partial top-k lists.
+__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
+    const float* __restrict__ inter_val,
+    const int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
+    float* __restrict__ out_val,
+    long long* __restrict__ out_idx,
+    int k, int bpr) {
+

import torch, time
import solution as S

def ref_topk(x, k):
    # reference via a non-forbidden manual path for smoke only (sort is fine in scratch, not solution.py)
    v, i = torch.topk(x, k, dim=-1, largest=True, sorted=True)
    return v, i

shapes = [(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
dev='cuda'
for (b,n,k) in shapes:
    S.batch, S.n, S.k = b,n,k
    m = S.Model(b,n,k).to(dev).eval()
    torch.manual_seed(0)
    x = torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    with torch.no_grad():
        sv, si = m(x)
    rv, ri = ref_topk(x,k)
    # value check
    dv = (sv.float()-rv.float()).abs().max().item()
    # gather check
    g = torch.gather(x, -1, si.to(torch.int64))
    dg = (g.float()-rv.float()).abs().max().item()
    print(f"shape b={b} n={n} k={k} bpr={m.bpr} T={m.threads}  max|dv|={dv:.3e}  max|gather-ref|={dg:.3e}")
print("SMOKE OK")

assistant
Baseline is `0.0091` (LOW) — and the timings reveal two problems: large-k shapes (0: 800µs, 2: 625µs) are catastrophically compute-bound, and even small-k shapes carry a ~14µs launch-overhead floor. Root cause of the compute cliff: `MAXK=64` arrays with dynamic indexing spill to local memory, and the insertion bubble's runtime index forces local memory regardless of k. The fix is to template on K and use a **register-resident predicated insertion** (data-independent, compile-time indices → registers, no local-memory spill). Let me rewrite.

 ------
 The deck is bandwidth/launch bound: each row read is tiny (0.5-2 MB), so the
 wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel-launch + dispatch overhead, not by the
-selection compute. Two levers:
-
-  1. A lean single custom kernel (block-per-row) that reads each element once
-     and keeps a per-thread local top-k, then a shared-memory merge-tree
-     reduces the block to its top-k.  For the single very-large row
-     (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot saturate DRAM, so the row is split
-     across BPR blocks (each emits a partial top-k) and a second tiny kernel
-     merges the BPR partials.

+selection compute. Levers:
+
+  1. A lean custom kernel (block-per-row, templated on K). Each thread keeps a
+     register-resident sorted top-K buffer, updated with a *branchless,
+     compile-time-indexed* insertion so the buffer never spills to local
+     memory. A shared-memory merge-tree reduces the block to its top-K.
+     For the single very-large row (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot
+     saturate DRAM, so the row is split across BPR blocks (each emits a partial
+     top-K) and a second tiny kernel merges the partials.
+
+  2. Reusable output buffers (allocated once per Model) plus CUDA-graph
      capture/replay, which collapses per-call launch + Python dispatch overhead
      to a single graph launch -- the dominant cost on these shapes.

 #include <cuda_runtime.h>

-// Merge two descending top-k lists (A,B) -> top-k of the union, into (ov,oi).
+// Branchless insert of (v, idx) into a descending register-resident top-K
+// buffer (drops the current min). All indices are compile-time so tv/ti stay
+// in registers.
+template <int K>
+__device__ __forceinline__ void insert(float* tv, int* ti, float v, int idx) {
+    if (v <= tv[K - 1]) return;
+    float pv = v;  int pi = idx;
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int p = 0; p < K; ++p) {
+        bool take = (pv > tv[p]);
+        float nv = take ? pv : tv[p];   int ni = take ? pi : ti[p];
+        float dv = take ? tv[p] : pv;   int di = take ? ti[p] : pi;
+        tv[p] = nv; ti[p] = ni; pv = dv; pi = di;
+    }
+}
+

cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > scratch_micro.py <<'EOF'
import torch, solution as S
dev='cuda'
# Force bpr=1, k=8: small n single block
def run(b,n,k,force_bpr=None,force_T=None):
    m = S.Model(b,n,k).to(dev).eval()
    if force_bpr is not None: m.bpr=force_bpr
    if force_T is not None: m.threads=force_T
    m._ready=False
    torch.manual_seed(1)
    x = torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    with torch.no_grad(): sv,si=m(x)
    rv,ri=torch.topk(x,k,dim=-1)
    dv=(sv.float()-rv.float()).abs().max().item()
    g=torch.gather(x,-1,si.to(torch.int64))
    dg=(g.float()-rv.float()).abs().max().item()
    print(f"b={b} n={n} k={k} bpr={m.bpr} T={m.threads}: max|dv|={dv:.3e} gather={dg:.3e}")
    if dv>1e-3:
        print("  ref[0,:k]=",rv[0,:min(k,8)].tolist())
        print("  sol[0,:k]=",sv[0,:min(k,8)].tolist())

run(1,256,8,force_bpr=1,force_T=32)   # k>1, bpr=1, single block
run(1,256,8,force_bpr=2,force_T=32)   # k>1, bpr=2, multiblock
run(2,64,1,force_bpr=2,force_T=16)    # k=1, bpr=2
EOF

--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/.claude/projects/-home-infatoshi-kernelbench-com/memory/kbhard-topk-3090.md
@@ -0,0 +1,32 @@
+---
+name: kbhard-topk-3090
+description: 05_topk_bitonic on 3090 is launch-overhead-bound; CUDA graphs + templated register top-k are the wins
+metadata:
+  type: project
+---
+
+05_topk_bitonic graded on RTX 3090 (peak_bandwidth 936 GB/s, geomean of
+gbps/936 over 5 shapes). Reads are tiny (0.5-2 MB/shape) so wall-clock is
+dominated by kernel-launch + Python dispatch overhead, NOT bandwidth — even a
+trivial k=1 kernel over 2 MB floors at ~13-14 us (pure overhead). The memory
+note "topk ~0.02 ceiling, launch-overhead-bound" is exactly this.
+
+Key facts learned:
+- Competitors (glm-5.2, deepseek, minimax in concurrent runs) all do raw
+  per-call kernel launches with fresh torch.empty outputs — none use CUDA
+  graphs. That is the edge: capture once per input pointer, replay.
+- Templating the kernel on K and using register-resident top-k (compile-time
+  indices only) is essential. MAXK=64 dynamic-indexed local arrays spill to
+  local memory -> shape0 (k=64) took 800us; templated -> ~100us.
+- BUG that cost an hour: branchless merge `i += ta?1:0` in the two-pointer
+  merge silently fails to advance under -O3 (returns max replicated k times for
+  k>1, correct for k=1). Use the branchy `if(a>=b){..;++i;}else{..;++j;}` form.
+- check.py is positional value-match (sorted desc) + lenient gather-at-indices;
+  numeric stress = input*1e-4 (atol 1e-7) and *1e3 — trivially passed since we
+  return exact selected values.
+- CUDA-graph correctness across check.py: replay reads live memory at the
+  captured x pointer, so pointer-reuse with new data is still correct; only
+  re-capture when x.data_ptr()/shape changes.
+
+Progression: naive multilaunch local-mem 0.009 -> templated register 0.038.
+See [[kbhard-run-can-land-on-3090]].

+    def _run(self, x: torch.Tensor):
         _mod.topk_forward(
             x, self.out_val, self.out_idx, self.inter_val, self.inter_idx,
             self.batch, self.n, self.k, self.bpr, self.threads,
         )
+
+    def _capture(self, x: torch.Tensor):
+        # Warm up on a side stream (PyTorch CUDA-graph capture protocol), then
+        # record the kernel launches into a graph that reads from x's pointer
+        # and writes the reusable output buffers.
+        s = torch.cuda.Stream()
+        s.wait_stream(torch.cuda.current_stream())
+        with torch.cuda.stream(s):
+            for _ in range(2):
+                self._run(x)
+        torch.cuda.current_stream().wait_stream(s)
+        self._x_ref = x  # keep the captured input alive
+        g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
+        with torch.cuda.graph(g):
+            self._run(x)
+        self._graph = g
+
+    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor):
+        if not self._ready:
+            self._alloc(x.device)
+
+        if not (self._use_graph and x.is_cuda):
+            self._run(x)
+            return self.out_val, self.out_idx
+
+        key = (x.data_ptr(), tuple(x.shape))
+        if self._graph_key != key:
+            try:
+                self._capture(x)
+                self._graph_key = key
+            except Exception:
+                # Capture failed -> fall back to eager launches for good.
+                self._use_graph = False
+                self._graph = None
+                self._run(x)
+                return self.out_val, self.out_idx
+        self._graph.replay()
         return self.out_val, self.out_idx

cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > scratch_prof.py <<'EOF'
import torch, solution as S
dev='cuda'
shapes=[(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
def bench(fn, iters=200, warmup=30):
    for _ in range(warmup): fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    # back-to-back (amortized, no per-iter sync) -> kernel throughput
    s=torch.cuda.Event(True); e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
    s.record()
    for _ in range(iters): fn()
    e.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
    amort=s.elapsed_time(e)/iters
    # per-call with sync (like benchmark) -> includes launch/idle overhead
    ts=[]
    for _ in range(iters):
        torch.cuda.synchronize()
        s=torch.cuda.Event(True); e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
        s.record(); fn(); e.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        ts.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    ts.sort(); per=ts[len(ts)//2]
    return amort, per
for (b,n,k) in shapes:
    S.batch,S.n,S.k=b,n,k
    m=S.Model(b,n,k).to(dev).eval(); m._ready=False
    torch.manual_seed(7); x=torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    with torch.no_grad(): m(x)  # warm/capture
    using_graph = m._graph is not None and m._use_graph
    a,p=bench(lambda: m(x))
    bytes_in=b*n*4
    print(f"b={b} n={n} k={k} bpr={m.bpr} T={m.threads} graph={using_graph}: amort={a*1e3:.2f}us  percall={p*1e3:.2f}us  amortGBs={bytes_in/(a*1e-3)/1e9:.0f}")
EOF

Critical insight from profiling: **amort ≈ percall**, so launch overhead is no longer dominant — the kernels themselves are slow and compute/occupancy-bound. The amortized bandwidth collapses with k: shape0(k64)=7 GB/s, shape2(k32)=44, shape3(k16)=45, shape1(k8)=125, shape4(k1)=381. Large-k shapes spill registers (tv+ti+merge-temp = 4K registers); small-k shapes are grid-size-starved (only 128 blocks). Graphs are working (graph=True) and give a real ~2-3µs constant win that matters once kernels are fast. Let me sweep (T, bpr) configs empirically to find occupancy sweet spots before rewriting the large-k path.

}
command (1769 chars)
cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > scratch_sweep.py <<'EOF'
import torch, solution as S
dev='cuda'
mod=S._mod
def amort(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T,iters=150):
    fn=lambda: mod.topk_forward(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
    for _ in range(20): fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    s=torch.cuda.Event(True);e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
    s.record()
    for _ in range(iters): fn()
    e.record();torch.cuda.synchronize()
    return s.elapsed_time(e)/iters
def npow2(v):
    p=1
    while p<v: p<<=1
    return p
shapes=[(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
for (b,n,k) in shapes:
    ov=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
    oi=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.int64,device=dev)
    torch.manual_seed(7); x=torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    best=(1e9,None)
    res=[]
    for T in [32,64,128,256,512]:
        if T*k*8>48000: continue
        for bpr in [1,2,4,8,16,32,64,128]:
            if bpr*k*8>48000: continue
            if b*bpr>4096*8: continue
            if n//bpr < 1: continue
            iv=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
            ii=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.int32,device=dev)
            try:
                t=amort(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
            except Exception as ex:
                continue
            gb=b*n*4/(t*1e-3)/1e9
            res.append((gb,T,bpr,t))
            if t<best[0]: best=(t,(T,bpr))
    res.sort(reverse=True)
    print(f"=== b={b} n={n} k={k}: best {best[1]} ===")
    for gb,T,bpr,t in res[:6]:
        print(f"   T={T:4d} bpr={bpr:3d}  {t*1e3:7.2f}us  {gb:5.0f} GB/s")
EOF

import torch
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
src=open('solution.py').read()
import re
m=re.search(r'_CUDA_SRC = r"""(.*?)"""', src, re.S)
cuda=m.group(1)
decl=("void topk_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor out_val, torch::Tensor out_idx, "

print("built")

assistant
No register spills at all — the report shows large-k kernels use 151-198 registers but spill 0 bytes. So the large-k slowness is **occupancy starvation**: for k=64, the merge buffer needs `T*K*8 = 32KB` shared → only 1 block/SM with just 2 warps. That's the real bottleneck, not compute. The fix is a **warp-shuffle merge** (reduce 32 lanes' top-K with no shared), cutting shared from `T*K` to `(T/32)*K` — 32× less. Let me check the float4 result first.

         float a = Av[i], b = Bv[j];
         if (a >= b) { ov[m] = a; oi[m] = Ai[i]; ++i; }
         else        { ov[m] = b; oi[m] = Bi[j]; ++j; }

+}
+
+// Warp reduction: 32 lanes each hold a sorted top-K in registers; butterfly
+// shuffle-merge so lane 0 ends with the warp-wide top-K. No shared memory.
+template <int K>
+__device__ __forceinline__ void warp_merge(float* tv, int* ti) {
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
+        float rv[K]; int ri[K];
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) {
+            rv[m] = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, tv[m], off);
+            ri[m] = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffffu, ti[m], off);
+        }
+        float ov[K]; int oi[K];
+        merge2<K>(tv, ti, rv, ri, ov, oi);
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = ov[m]; ti[m] = oi[m]; }
     }
 }

cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > scratch_sweep.py <<'EOF'
import torch, solution as S
dev='cuda'; mod=S._mod
def amort(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T,iters=120):
    fn=lambda: mod.topk_forward(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
    for _ in range(15): fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    s=torch.cuda.Event(True);e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
    s.record()
    for _ in range(iters): fn()
    e.record();torch.cuda.synchronize()
    return s.elapsed_time(e)/iters
shapes=[(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
for (b,n,k) in shapes:
    ov=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
    oi=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.int64,device=dev)
    torch.manual_seed(7); x=torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    res=[]
    for T in [32,64,128,256,512,1024]:
        if (T//32)*k*8>48000: continue
        for bpr in [1,2,4,8,16,32,64,128,256]:
            if bpr*k*8>48000: continue
            if (n//bpr) < T: continue   # need >=1 elem per thread roughly
            if b*bpr>4096: continue
            iv=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
            ii=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.int32,device=dev)
            try: t=amort(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
            except Exception: continue
            res.append((b*n*4/(t*1e-3)/1e9,T,bpr,t))
    res.sort(reverse=True)
    print(f"=== b={b} n={n} k={k} ===")
    for gb,T,bpr,t in res[:5]:
        print(f"   T={T:4d} bpr={bpr:3d}  {t*1e3:7.2f}us  {gb:5.0f} GB/s")
EOF

Critical measurement flaw caught: my `amort` profiling reads x back-to-back so it stays L2-cached (6MB L2), measuring L2 bandwidth not cold DRAM. `benchmark.py` flushes L2 before each call. So `bpr=1` looks great on L2 (no merge overhead) but for cold DRAM, one block on one SM can't saturate 936 GB/s — I need many blocks. Let me re-profile **with L2 flush** to match the real benchmark, and cap T by register limit.

command (1989 chars)
cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > scratch_sweep2.py <<'EOF'
import torch, statistics, solution as S
dev='cuda'; mod=S._mod
flush=torch.empty(128*1024*1024//4,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
def timed(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T,iters=40):
    fn=lambda: mod.topk_forward(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
    for _ in range(12): fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    ts=[]
    for _ in range(iters):
        flush.zero_(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        s=torch.cuda.Event(True);e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
        s.record(); fn(); e.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        ts.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    return statistics.median(ts)
regs={1:16,8:40,16:59,32:102,64:198}  # conservative (merge kernel regs)
shapes=[(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
for (b,n,k) in shapes:
    ov=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
    oi=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.int64,device=dev)
    torch.manual_seed(7); x=torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    res=[]
    for T in [64,128,256,512]:
        if T*regs[k]>65000: continue
        if (T//32)*k*8>48000: continue
        for bpr in [1,2,4,8,16,32,64,128]:
            if bpr*k*8>48000: continue
            if (n//bpr) < T: continue
            if b*bpr>4096: continue
            iv=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
            ii=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.int32,device=dev)
            try:
                t=timed(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T); torch.cuda.synchronize()
            except Exception: 
                torch.cuda.synchronize(); continue
            res.append((b*n*4/(t*1e-3)/1e9,T,bpr,t))
    res.sort(reverse=True)
    print(f"=== b={b} n={n} k={k} (L2-flushed) ===")
    for gb,T,bpr,t in res[:6]:
        print(f"   T={T:4d} bpr={bpr:3d}  {t*1e3:7.2f}us  {gb:5.0f} GB/s  frac={gb/936:.3f}")
EOF

+// same warp + cross-warp reduction yields the row's final top-K.

 __global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
     const float* __restrict__ inter_val, const int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
     float* __restrict__ out_val, long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int bpr) {

+        #pragma unroll

+        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = -FLT_MAX; ti[m] = 0; }

cat > scratch_gsweep.py <<'EOF'
import torch, statistics, solution as S
dev='cuda'; mod=S._mod
flush=torch.empty(128*1024*1024//4,dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
def cap_time(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T,iters=50):
    fn=lambda: mod.topk_forward(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T)
    s=torch.cuda.Stream(); s.wait_stream(torch.cuda.current_stream())
    with torch.cuda.stream(s):
        for _ in range(3): fn()
    torch.cuda.current_stream().wait_stream(s)
    g=torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
    with torch.cuda.graph(g): fn()
    for _ in range(5): g.replay()
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    ts=[]
    for _ in range(iters):
        flush.zero_(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        a=torch.cuda.Event(True);e=torch.cuda.Event(True)
        a.record(); g.replay(); e.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        ts.append(a.elapsed_time(e))
    return statistics.median(ts)
regs={1:16,8:40,16:59,32:102,64:200}
shapes=[(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(128,4096,1)]
cfgs={
 (1,131072,64):[(64,16),(64,32),(64,64),(128,16),(128,32),(256,8),(256,16),(128,64)],
 (64,8192,8):[(128,1),(256,1),(128,2),(256,2),(128,4),(64,2)],
 (32,16384,32):[(128,1),(256,1),(128,2),(128,4),(256,2),(64,4)],
 (16,12000,16):[(128,2),(128,4),(64,4),(64,8),(256,2),(128,8)],
 (128,4096,1):[(256,1),(512,1),(128,1),(256,2),(128,2)],
}
for sh in shapes:
    b,n,k=sh
    ov=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
    oi=torch.empty((b,k),dtype=torch.int64,device=dev)
    torch.manual_seed(7); x=torch.randn(b,n,device=dev)
    res=[]
    for (T,bpr) in cfgs[sh]:
        if T*regs[k]>65000: continue
        iv=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.float32,device=dev)
        ii=torch.empty(max(1,b*bpr*k),dtype=torch.int32,device=dev)
        try: t=cap_time(x,ov,oi,iv,ii,b,n,k,bpr,T); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        except Exception as ex: torch.cuda.synchronize(); print("  skip",T,bpr,str(ex)[:40]); continue
        res.append((b*n*4/(t*1e-3)/1e9,T,bpr,t))
    res.sort(reverse=True)
    print(f"=== b={b} n={n} k={k} (graph+L2flush) ===", flush=True)
    for gb,T,bpr,t in res:
        print(f"   T={T:4d} bpr={bpr:3d}  {t*1e3:7.2f}us  {gb:5.0f} GB/s  frac={gb/936:.3f}", flush=True)

PASS at 0.0433. The fraction collapses with k (k1:0.24, k8:0.115, k16/k32:0.035, k64:0.004), pointing squarely at `warp_merge` register cost growing with K — for k=64 the two-pointer merge needs 6×K=384 registers and spills. Let me replace it with a **register-frugal in-place bitonic merge** (4×K registers: shuffle partner in, `max(A[i],B[K-1-i])` → bitonic, then bitonic sort). This should unspill k=64 and speed up k16/k32 too.

+// Warp reduction: 32 lanes each hold a descending top-K in registers; butterfly
+// shuffle so lane 0 ends with the warp-wide top-K.  Each step merges two
+// descending K-lists in place via the bitonic top-K trick
+// (C[i] = max(A[i], B[K-1-i]) is bitonic and holds the top-K; bitonic-sort it),
+// which needs only the received list as scratch (4K regs, no 6K two-pointer).

 __device__ __forceinline__ void warp_merge(float* tv, int* ti) {
     #pragma unroll

diff (38 lines)
--- /dev/null
+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_142752_claude_claude-opus-4-8_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic/scratch_ceiling.py
@@ -0,0 +1,35 @@
+"""Practical cold-read bandwidth ceiling per shape (torch reduction proxy),
+measured the same way benchmark.py times: L2 flush + CUDA graph + per-call sync.
+Tells us how close a *pure read* of each shape gets to 936 GB/s, i.e. the best
+any top-k kernel could hope for given the tiny transfer sizes."""
+import torch, statistics
+dev = 'cuda'
+flush = torch.empty(128 * 1024 * 1024 // 4, dtype=torch.float32, device=dev)
+shapes = [(1, 131072, 64), (64, 8192, 8), (32, 16384, 32), (16, 12000, 16), (128, 4096, 1)]
+
+
+def cap_time(fn, iters=50):
+    s = torch.cuda.Stream(); s.wait_stream(torch.cuda.current_stream())
+    with torch.cuda.stream(s):
+        for _ in range(3): fn()
+    torch.cuda.current_stream().wait_stream(s)
+    g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
+    with torch.cuda.graph(g): fn()
+    for _ in range(5): g.replay()
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    ts = []
+    for _ in range(iters):
+        flush.zero_(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        a = torch.cuda.Event(True); e = torch.cuda.Event(True)
+        a.record(); g.replay(); e.record(); torch.cuda.synchronize()
+        ts.append(a.elapsed_time(e))
+    return statistics.median(ts)
+
+
+for (b, n, k) in shapes:
+    torch.manual_seed(7); x = torch.randn(b, n, device=dev)
+    out = torch.empty(b, device=dev)
+    def fn(x=x, out=out): torch.sum(x, dim=-1, out=out)
+    t = cap_time(fn)
+    gb = b * n * 4 / (t * 1e-3) / 1e9
+    print(f"b={b} n={n} k={k}: sum(dim=-1) {t*1e3:6.2f}us  {gb:5.0f} GB/s  frac={gb/936:.3f}", flush=True)

  "content": "<1485 chars \u2014 see diff>"

10	05_topk_bitonic scored on RTX 3090 (936 GB/s DRAM). Achieved geomean
11	peak_fraction ~0.05 (RESULT: LOW vs the 0.1 generic threshold, but that
12	threshold is unreachable for top-k on 3090 — it is launch-overhead-bound:
13	every row is 16KB-512KB, so even a zero-work kernel bottoms out at ~11us
14	dispatch floor). torch.topk itself scores ~0.023 geomean; 0.05 is ~2.15x it.
15	
16	Per-shape (mine / torch.topk us): shape0 (1,131072,64)=54/68,
17	shape1 (64,8192,8)=19/71, shape2 (32,16384,32)=40/71, shape3 (16,12000,16)=30/66,
18	shape4 (128,4096,1)=14/41. Beats torch.topk on every shape.
19	
20	Winning design (shape-adaptive):
21	- k<=16: per-row REGISTER cascade. One block/row; each thread keeps a size-K
22	  sorted-desc register buffer, merged across the block by a log2(BLOCK) merge-tree
23	  in shmem (stride K+1 to dodge 32-way bank conflicts). CRITICAL: dynamic
24	  indexing into a register array spills to local memory (1389 .local refs,
25	  ~10x slower) — use a fully-unrolled conditional-cascade with STATIC indices.
26	  A shmem min-heap (O(logK)) is SLOWER than the O(K) register cascade because
27	  the sift-down's dependent shmem-load chain (~30cyc/level) beats 1cyc registers.
28	- k>=32: per

 Build gotcha: torch 2.11's List_inl.h is ill-formed under gcc>=14 (needs
 typename) — avoids this by compiling a standalone .so (extern "C", nvcc
 -ccbin g++-14) called via ctypes with raw data_ptr(), never including
-torch/extension.h. See [[kbhard-run-can-land-on-3090]].+torch/extension.h. See [[kbhard-run-can-land-on-3090]].
+
+UPDATE (2026-06-18 session, opus-4-8): NEW EDGE = CUDA graphs. Capture the
+kernel(s) into a torch.cuda.CUDAGraph keyed on x.data_ptr()+shape, replay on
+match (re-capture on ptr change). Correct across check.py because replay reads
+LIVE memory at the captured pointer — pointer reuse with new data still works.
+load_inline (torch/extension.h) compiles fine here (no gcc-14 issue this run);
+the standalone-.so dance was not needed. Graphs collapse the per-call dispatch
+floor, beating the prior session on the small-k shapes (k1 ~8.7us vs 14us).
+Kernel design this run: templated-on-K register top-k via BRANCHLESS predicated
+insert (compile-time indices = registers, no local spill) + float4 MLP loads +
+warp-shuffle reduction. For the warp reduction at large K, the two-pointer merge
+needs 6K registers and SPILLS at K=64 (-> 130us); replace with the in-place
+bitonic top-k merge C[i]=max(A[i],B[K-1-i]) then bitonic-sort (4K regs). STILL,
+the prior session's RADIX-256 select for k>=32 beat this per-thread-topk+merge
+on shape0/shape2 (radix 54/40us vs warp-merge 133/55us) — for large k, radix is
+the better algorithm; per-thread-topk wins only for small k. Ceiling ~0.05-0.06.
+BUG to avoid: branchless `i += cond?1:0` pointer-advance in a #pragma-unrolled
+two-pointer merge silently fails under -O3 (returns max repeated for k>1); use
+the branchy if/else form.

Key realization on shape0: the k64 `warp_merge` needs 4×K=256 registers (just over the 255 limit) → it **spills ~1 register to local memory, which is DRAM-backed**. On the L2-flushed cold path those spill accesses hit cold DRAM → catastrophic 133µs. That's why bitonic didn't help shape0. The fix: keep k64 off the spilling warp_merge. Let me first see the bitonic+MLP result.

 Design
 ------
 The deck is bandwidth/launch bound: each row read is tiny (0.5-2 MB), so the
-wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel-launch + dispatch overhead, not by the
-selection compute. Levers:
-
-  1. A lean custom kernel (block-per-row, templated on K). Each thread keeps a
-     register-resident sorted top-K buffer, updated with a *branchless,
-     compile-time-indexed* insertion so the buffer never spills to local
-     memory. A shared-memory merge-tree reduces the block to its top-K.
-     For the single very-large row (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot
-     saturate DRAM, so the row is split across BPR blocks (each emits a partial
-     top-K) and a second tiny kernel merges the partials.
+wall-clock floor is dominated by kernel launch/dispatch overhead and cold-DRAM
+latency, not the selection compute. Levers:
+
+  1. A custom kernel (block-per-row, templated on K). Each thread streams its
+     slice with vectorized float4 loads and keeps a register-resident sorted
+     top-K buffer, updated with a *branchless, compile-time-indexed* insertion
+     so the buffer never spills to local memory.
+       - K<=32: lanes are reduced by a warp-shuffle butterfly using an in-place
+         bitonic top-K merge (C[i]=max(A[i],B[K-1-i]) is bitonic; bitonic-sort
+         it), so only T/32 partials hit shared memory -> high occupancy.
+       - K==64: the warp bitonic merge would need 256 registers and spill to
+         (DRAM-backed) local memory, which is ruinous on the cold path, so the
+         block reduces all T lists through a shared-memory merge-tree instead.
+     For the single very-large row (batch=1, n=131072) one block cannot saturate
+     DRAM, so the row is split across BPR blocks (each emits a partial top-K)
+     and a second tiny kernel merges the partials.
 
   2. Reusable output buffers (allocated once per Model) plus CUDA-graph
      capture/replay, which collapses per-call launch + Python dispatch overhead
-     to a single graph launch -- the dominant cost on these shapes.
+     to a single graph launch. Replay reads live memory at the captured input
+     pointer, so it stays correct as the input data changes between calls.

221	// Merge kernel: grid = batch, blockDim = padded multiple of 32 >= bpr.
222	// Each thread loads one partial top-K list (padding lanes load -inf), then the
223	// same warp + cross-warp reduction yields the row's final top-K.
224	template <int K>
225	__global__ void topk_merge_kernel(
226	    const float* __restrict__ inter_val, const int* __restrict__ inter_idx,
227	    float* __restrict__ out_val, long long* __restrict__ out_idx, int bpr) {
228	
229	    extern __shared__ unsigned char smem[];
230	    int nlists = (K <= 32) ? ((blockDim.x >> 5) < 1 ? 1 : (blockDim.x >> 5)) : blockDim.x;
231	    float* sval = reinterpret_cast<float*>(smem);
232	    int*   sidx = reinterpret_cast<int*>(sval + nlists * K);
233	
234	    const int T = blockDim.x, tid = threadIdx.x, row = blockIdx.x;
235	
236	    float tv[K]; int ti[K];
237	    if (tid < bpr) {
238	        long long off = ((long long)row * bpr + tid) * K;
239	        #pragma unroll
240	        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = inter_val[off + m]; ti[m] = inter_idx[off + m]; }
241	    } else {
242	        #pragma unroll
243	        for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { tv[m] = -FLT_MAX; ti[m] = 0; }
244	    }
245	
246	    if constexpr (K <= 32) {
247	        warp_merge<K>(tv, ti);
248	        const int lane = tid & 31, warp = tid >> 5, W = T >> 5;
249	        if (lane == 0) {
250	            #pragma unroll
251	            for (int m = 0; m < K; ++m) { sval

368	    def _alloc(self, device):
369	        b, k, bpr = self.batch, self.k, self.bpr
370	        self.out_val = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
371	        self.out_idx = torch.empty((b, k), dtype=torch.int64, device=device)
372	        sz = b * bpr * k if bpr > 1 else 1
373	        self.inter_val = torch.empty(sz, dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
374	        self.inter_idx = torch.empty(sz, dtype=torch.int32, device=device)
375	        self._ready = True

377	    def _run(self, x: torch.Tensor):
378	        _mod.topk_forward(
379	            x, self.out_val, self.out_idx, self.inter_val, self.inter_idx,
380	            self.batch, self.n, self.k, self.bpr, self.threads,
381	        )
382	
383	    def _capture(self, x: torch.Tensor):
384	        # Warm up on a side stream (PyTorch CUDA-graph capture protocol), then
385	        # record the kernel launches into a graph that reads from x's pointer
386	        # and writes the reusable output buffers.
387	        s = torch.cuda.Stream()
388	        s.wait_stream(torch.cuda.current_stream())
389	        with torch.cuda.stream(s):
390	            for _ in range(2):
391	                self._run(x)
392	        torch.cuda.current_stream().wait_stream(s)
393	        self._x_ref = x  # keep the captured input alive
394	        g = torch.cuda.CUDAGraph()
395	        with torch.cuda.graph(g):
396	            self._run(x)
397	        self._graph = g
